Who is more common as the object form, especially in questions ÓëÖ®Ïà±È, whoµ¹³£ÓÃ×÷±öÓï, ÓÈÓÃì¶ÒÉÎÊ¾äÖĞ: Who did you see at the party? ÄãÔÚ¾Û»áÖĞ¿´¼ûË­ÁË? (Compound adjs formed from well- + past participles are usu hyphenated when attributive but not hyphenated when predicative, except when the adj has acquired a restricted sense. Who is more common as the object form, especially in questions ÓëÖ®Ïà±È, whoµ¹³£ÓÃ×÷±öÓï, ÓÈÓÃì¶ÒÉÎÊ¾äÖĞ: Who did you see at the party? ÄãÔÚ¾Û»áÖĞ¿´¼ûË­ÁË? The object pronoun is often omitted or replaced by who or that ÔÚÕâÖÖ´Ó¾äÖĞ, ±ö¸ñ´ú´Ê whom ÍùÍùÊ¡È¥²»ÓÃ, »òÓÃwho»òthat´úÖ®: The students(whom/who/that) we examined last week were excellent.
